<HEAD>
<TITLE>EX-10.11: EMPLOYMENT AGREEMENT</TITLE>
</HEAD>
<BODY bgcolor="#FFFFFF">
<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<!-- link2 "Exhibit&nbsp;10.17" -->
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Exhibit&nbsp;10.11</B>
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2"><B>BARNES &#038; NOBLE, INC.</B>
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2"><B>122 Fifth Avenue</B>
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2"><B>New York, New York 10011</B>
</FONT>

<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR valign="top">
        <TD width="50%"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD width="50%"><FONT size="2">As of February&nbsp;18, 2002</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P><FONT size="2">Mr.&nbsp;Mitchell S. Klipper<BR>
3 Clearmeadow Lane<BR>
Woodbury, New York 11797
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">Dear Mr.&nbsp;Klipper:
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This letter agreement is intended to set forth our mutual understanding
regarding your employment as Chief Operating Officer of Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc.
(the &#147;Company&#148;). Accordingly, we are pleased to agree as follows:
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Employment; Duties.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;You agree to be Chief Operating Officer of the
Company for the term of this Agreement. In this capacity you shall perform
such duties and have such responsibilities as are typically associated with the
office of Chief Operating Officer, including such duties and responsibilities
as are prescribed by the Board of Directors of the Company (the &#147;Board&#148;)
consistent with the office of Chief Operating Officer. While you are the
Company&#146;s employee, you agree to devote your full business time and attention
to the performance of your duties and responsibilities hereunder.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Term.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(a)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Unless terminated earlier in accordance with the provisions
set forth below, the term of this Agreement will be for a period beginning on
the date hereof and ending on the third anniversary of the date hereof. At the
expiration (but not earlier termination) of the term (including any renewal
term), the term of this Agreement shall automatically renew for an additional
period of one year, unless either party has given the other party written
notice of non-renewal at least one year prior to such renewal.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This Agreement shall terminate upon your death and may be terminated
by the Company by written notice to you following your Disability (as defined
below). This Agreement may also be terminated by the Company for Cause (as
defined below) upon written notice to you. This Agreement may also be
terminated by you for Good Cause (as defined below) upon written notice to the
Company.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(c)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For purposes of this Agreement:
</FONT>

<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(i)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&#147;Cause&#148; shall mean (A)&nbsp;your final conviction of a felony
impacting on the performance of your duties or involving a crime of moral
turpitude, or (B)&nbsp;misappropriation or embezzlement in the performance of
your duties as an employee of the Company, or (C)&nbsp;willfully engaging in
conduct materially injurious to the Company and in violation of your
obligations under this Agreement, which violation </FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">continues for at least
30&nbsp;days after written notice thereof from the Company to you specifying
such violation in reasonable detail.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(ii)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&#147;Disability&#148; shall mean a written determination by a physician
mutually agreeable to the Company and you (or, in the event of your total
physical or mental disability, your legal representative) that you are
physically or mentally unable to perform your duties of Chief Operating
Officer under this Agreement and that such disability can reasonably
be expected to continue for a period of six consecutive months or
for shorter periods aggregating 180&nbsp;days in any 12-month period.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Compensation.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Salary.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company will pay you, for all services you perform
hereunder, an annual salary of $600,000, or such higher amount as the
Compensation Committee of the Board (the &#147;Compensation Committee&#148;) may
determine, payable in accordance with the Company&#146;s payroll schedule applicable
to executive officers of the Company.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Bonus Compensation.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition to your above-mentioned salary, we
will pay you, within 90&nbsp;days following the end of each fiscal year of the
Company during the term of your employment, annual bonus compensation in an
amount determined in accordance with the Company&#146;s Supplemental Compensation
Plan. We agree that for the entire term hereof, you shall be entitled to
participate in that plan.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Employee Benefits.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the term of your employment, you will
participate in and receive any benefits to which you are entitled under
employee benefit plans which the Company provides for all employees, as well as
all benefits which the Company provides, or may at any time in the future
provide, for its executive officers.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Expenses; Car Allowance.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the term of your employment, we
will: (a)&nbsp;pay you a car allowance per month of $1,500, or such higher amount
as may be determined by the Compensation Committee; and (b)&nbsp;reimburse you for
all expenses incurred by you in the performance of your duties and
responsibilities under this Agreement, including, without limitation,
entertainment and travel expenses, in accordance with the policies and
procedures established by the Compensation Committee.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Life and Disability Insurance.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition to the foregoing, we will
obtain in your name a life insurance policy providing for a death benefit of
$1,000,000 payable to any beneficiary or beneficiaries named by you, and a
disability insurance policy providing for monthly payments to you of at least
$12,800 during the period of any disability until the earlier of your attaining
age 65 or death. During the term of your employment, we will pay all premiums
due on such policies.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.6.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Severance.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In the event of the expiration or termination of the term
of your employment (other than for Cause, your death or Disability, or your
voluntary termination of your employment, whether through resignation,
non-renewal or otherwise), we will pay you a lump sum, within 30&nbsp;days following
such expiration or termination, equal to (a)&nbsp;the sum of (i)&nbsp;your then annual
salary, (ii)&nbsp;your annual bonus for the then most recently completed fiscal year
of the Company, and (iii)&nbsp;the then aggregate annual dollar amount of the
</FONT><P align="center"><FONT size="2">2</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<P align="left"><FONT size="2">payments made or to be made by the Company for purposes of providing you with
the benefits set forth in paragraphs 3.3 through 3.5 above, multiplied by (b)
the greater of (i)&nbsp;two or (ii)&nbsp;the number of months remaining in the term of
this Agreement divided by 12. You shall be under no duty to mitigate damages
and the amount paid to you under this paragraph 3.6 shall not be diminished in
any way by your earnings or income from any other sources.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.7.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Stock Options.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Effective as of the date hereof, you shall be granted
stock options to purchase 275,000 shares of common stock of the Company at an
exercise price of $29.50 per share. Between the date hereof and the earliest
date hereafter that the stockholders of the Company adopt a new stock option
plan or increase the number of shares issuable under options granted under any
of the Company&#146;s existing stock option plans (the &#147;New Plan Date&#148;), you may be
granted additional stock options to purchase shares of common stock of the
Company at an exercise price of not more than $29.50 per share. Effective as
of the New Plan Date, you shall be granted stock options to purchase that
number of shares of common stock of the Company which, when added to all
other grants to you under this Section&nbsp;3.7, equals 800,000 shares, at an
exercise price of not more than $29.50 per share unless you otherwise agree;
provided, however, that the maximum number of shares for which you will be
granted options to purchase in any calendar year shall not exceed 700,000, and
any options which would otherwise have been granted to you but for such
limitation shall be granted to you in the next calendar year. All options
granted to you under this Section&nbsp;3.7 shall expire on the earlier of (a)&nbsp;the
tenth anniversary of the date hereof and (b)&nbsp;one year after the expiration or
earlier termination (other than for Cause) of the term of your employment,
unless otherwise extended by the Compensation Committee. Such options shall
vest and be exercisable in equal one-fourth increments on the first through
fourth anniversaries of the date hereof, respectively. Notwithstanding the
foregoing, all such options shall vest and be immediately exercisable in full
upon a Change of Control (as defined below) or upon the earlier expiration or
termination of this Agreement (unless such earlier termination is for Cause or
results from your voluntary termination of your employment).
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.8.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Change of Control Payments.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(a)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If at any time during the term of
this Agreement there is a Change of Control and (i)&nbsp;your employment is
terminated by the Company for any reason (other than for Cause) or (ii)&nbsp;you
voluntarily terminate your employment for Good Cause, in either case within the
greater of two years following the Change of Control or the remaining term of
this Agreement, the Company shall pay to you the following amount: (A)&nbsp;the sum
of (x)&nbsp;your then annual salary, (y)&nbsp;your then most recent annual bonus, and (z)
the then aggregate annual dollar amount of the payments made or to be made by
the Company for purposes of providing you with the benefits set forth in
paragraphs 3.3 through 3.6 above, multiplied by (B)&nbsp;the greater of (x)&nbsp;three or
(y)&nbsp;the number of months remaining in the term of this Agreement divided by 12;
provided that the maximum amount payable pursuant to this Section&nbsp;3.8 shall be
the maximum amount payable to the Executive without triggering an excise tax
under Section&nbsp;280G of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended, or any
successor provision thereto. The amount due under this Section&nbsp;3.8 shall be
paid to you in one lump sum within 30&nbsp;days after the date your employment
terminates. Subject to the Section&nbsp;280G limitation referred to above, to the
extent that you are not fully vested in any retirement benefits from any
pension, profit-sharing or other retirement plan or program maintained by the
Company, the Company shall pay directly to you the difference between the
amounts which would have been paid to you had you been fully vested on the date
that your employment
</FONT><P align="center"><FONT size="2">3</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<P align="left"><FONT size="2">terminates and the amounts actually paid or payable to you
pursuant to such plans or programs. The amounts payable to you under this
Section&nbsp;3.8 shall be in lieu of any amounts payable to you under Section&nbsp;3.6
above.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(b)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As used herein, &#147;Change of Control&#148; shall mean the occurrence of one
or more of the following events:
</FONT>

<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(i)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;after the date hereof, any person, entity or &#147;group&#148; as
identified in Sections&nbsp;13(d)(3) or 14(d)(2) of the Securities Exchange
Act of 1934 (the &#147;1934 Act&#148;), other than you or any of your affiliates or
Leonard Riggio or any of his heirs or affiliates, becomes a beneficial
owner (as such term is defined in Rule&nbsp;13d-3 under the 1934 Act) directly
or indirectly of securities representing 40% or more of the total number
of votes that may be cast for the election of directors of the Company;
or</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(ii)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within two years after a merger, consolidation, liquidation or
sale of assets involving the Company, or a contested election of a
Company director, or any combination of the foregoing, the individuals
who were directors of the Company immediately prior thereto shall cease
to constitute a majority of the Board; or</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(iii)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within two years after a tender offer or exchange offer for
voting securities of the Company, the individuals who were directors of
the Company immediately prior thereto shall cease to constitute a
majority of the Board.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(c)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As used herein, &#147;Good Cause&#148; shall mean the occurrence of one or more
of the following events within two years after a Change of Control:
</FONT>

<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(i)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there shall have been a material modification of your duties,
title or direct reports;</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(ii)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there shall have been a material reduction in the compensation
and benefits you receive from the Company; or</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P>
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR>
        <TD width="9%"></TD>
        <TD width="91%"></TD>
</TR>
<TR valign="top">
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(iii)&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the principal executive offices of the Company shall be
relocated to a location outside of the New York City metropolitan area.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Non-Competition.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Covenant.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;You agree that so long as you are employed by the Company
and for a period of two years thereafter, you will not directly or indirectly,
either as principal, agent, stockholder, employee or in any other capacity,
engage in or have a financial interest in any business that is competitive with
the businesses operated by the Company or any of its subsidiaries. The
foregoing provision shall cease to apply after: (i)&nbsp;you voluntary terminate
your employment for Good Cause within two years following a Change of Control;
or (ii)&nbsp;your employment terminates involuntarily, other than for Cause prior to
a Change of Control.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ownership of Other Securities.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nothing in paragraph 4.1 shall be
construed as denying you the right to own securities of any corporation listed
on a national
</FONT><P align="center"><FONT size="2">4</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<P align="left"><FONT size="2">securities exchange or quoted in the NASDAQ System to the extent
of an aggregate of 5% of the outstanding shares of such securities.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Reasonableness.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;You acknowledge that the foregoing limitations are
reasonable and properly required by the Company and that in the event that any
such limitations are found to be unreasonable by a court of competent
jurisdiction, you will submit to the reduction of such limitations as the court
shall find reasonable.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Severability.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If any of the restrictions in paragraph 4.1 should for
any reason whatsoever be declared invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction,
the validity or enforceability of the remainder of this Agreement will not be
adversely affected thereby.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;4.5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Equitable Relief.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;You acknowledge that your services to the Company
are of a unique character which give them a special value to the Company. You
further recognize that any violation of the restrictions in paragraph 4.1 may
give rise to losses or damages for which the Company cannot be reasonably or
adequately compensated in an action at law and that such violation may result
in irreparable and continuing harm to the Company. Accordingly, you agree
that, in addition to any other remedy which the Company may have at law or in
equity, the Company shall be entitled to injunctive relief to restrain any
violation by you of the restrictions in paragraph 4.1.
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Indemnification.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;You shall be indemnified by the Company, as an
officer and director of the Company and its affiliates, against all actions,
suits, claims, legal proceedings and the like to the fullest extent permitted
by law, including advancement of expenses, partial indemnification,
indemnification following the termination of this Agreement, indemnification of
your estate and similar matters.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Miscellaneous.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Entire Agreement.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This Agreement constitutes the entire agreement
between you and the Company with respect to the terms and conditions of your
employment by the Company and supersedes all prior agreements, understandings
and arrangements, oral or written, between you and the Company with respect to
the subject matter hereof.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Binding Effect; Benefits.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This Agreement shall inure to the benefit
of and shall be binding upon you and the Company and our respective heirs,
legal representatives, successors and assigns.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Amendments and Waivers.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This Agreement may not be amended or
modified except by an instrument or instruments in writing signed by the party
against whom enforcement of any such modification or amendment is sought.
Either party may, by an instrument in writing, waive compliance by the other
party with any term or provision of this Agreement to be performed or complied
with by such other party.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.4.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Assignment.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Neither this Agreement nor any rights or obligations
which either party may have by reason of this Agreement shall be assignable by
either party without the prior written consent of the other party.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">5</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>



<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.5.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Litigation Expenses.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company will pay any actual expenses for
reasonable attorneys&#146; fees and disbursements incurred by you, or your personal
representative, in seeking to obtain or enforce any right or benefit under this
Agreement, if you or your representative is the prevailing party.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.6.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;No Mitigation.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In the event of termination of this Agreement by you
as a result of the breach by the Company of any of its obligations hereunder,
or in the event of the termination of your employment by the Company in breach
of this Agreement, you shall not be required to seek other employment in order
to mitigate damages hereunder.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.7.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Notices.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Any notice which may or must be given under this Agreement
shall be in writing and shall be personally delivered or sent by certified or
registered mail, postage prepaid, or reputable overnight courier, addressed to
you or the Company, as the case may be, at the address set forth on the first
page hereof, or to such other address as you or the Company, as the case may
be, may designate in writing in accordance with the provisions of this
paragraph.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.8.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Section and Other Headings.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The section and other headings contained
in this Agreement are for reference purposes only and are not deemed to be a
part of this Agreement or to affect the meaning and interpretation of this
Agreement.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.9.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Governing Law.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This Agreement shall be construed (both as to
validity and performance) and enforced in accordance with and governed by the
laws of the State of New York applicable to agreements made and to be performed
wholly within the State of New York.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;6.10.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Survival of Rights and Obligations.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All rights and obligations of
you and the Company arising during the term of this Agreement shall continue to
have full force and effect after the termination of this Agreement unless
otherwise provided herein.
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If the foregoing accurately reflects our agreement, kindly sign and return
to us the enclosed duplicate copy of this letter.
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The selected consolidated financial data of Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc. and its

should be read in conjunction with the consolidated financial statements and
notes included elsewhere in this report. The Company&#146;s fiscal year is comprised
of 52 or 53&nbsp;weeks, ending on the Saturday closest to the last day of January.
The Statement of Operations Data for the 52&nbsp;weeks ended February&nbsp;2, 2002
(fiscal 2001), 53&nbsp;weeks ended February&nbsp;3, 2001 (fiscal 2000) and the 52&nbsp;weeks
ended January&nbsp;29, 2000 (fiscal 1999) and the Balance Sheet Data as of February
2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001 are derived from, and are qualified by reference
to, audited consolidated financial statements which are included elsewhere in
this report. The Statement of Operations Data for the 52&nbsp;weeks ended January
30, 1999 (fiscal 1998) and the 52&nbsp;weeks ended January&nbsp;31, 1998 (fiscal 1997)
and the Balance Sheet Data as of January&nbsp;29, 2000, January&nbsp;30, 1999 and January
31, 1998 are derived from audited consolidated financial statements not
included in this report. Certain prior-period amounts have been reclassified
for comparative purposes.

equity interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com for the
first three quarters ended October&nbsp;31, 1998 (also
the effective date of the limited liability
company agreement), and a 50&nbsp;percent equity
interest beginning on November&nbsp;1, 1998 through
the end of the fiscal year. As a result of the
initial public offering (IPO)&nbsp;for the Barnes &#038;
Noble.com business on May&nbsp;25, 1999, the Company
and Bertelsmann each retained a 40&nbsp;percent
interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. Accordingly, the
Company&#146;s share in the net loss of Barnes &#038;
Noble.com for fiscal 1999 was based on a 50
percent equity interest from the beginning of
fiscal 1999 through May&nbsp;25, 1999 and 40&nbsp;percent
through the end of the fiscal year. In November
2000, Barnes &#038; Noble.com acquired Fatbrain.com,
Inc. (Fatbrain), the third largest online
bookseller. Barnes &#038; Noble.com issued shares of
its common stock to Fatbrain shareholders. As a
result of this merger, the Company and
Bertelsmann each retained an approximate 36
percent interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com.
Accordingly, the Company&#146;s share in the net loss
of Barnes &#038; Noble.com was 40&nbsp;percent from the
beginning of fiscal 2000 through November 2000
and approximately 36&nbsp;percent thereafter.</FONT></TD>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">4</FONT>



<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>MANAGEMENT&#146;S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF<BR>
OPERATIONS</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s fiscal year is comprised of 52 or 53&nbsp;weeks, ending on the
Saturday closest to the last day of January. As used in this section, &#147;fiscal
2001&#148; represents the 52&nbsp;weeks ended February&nbsp;2, 2002, &#147;fiscal 2000&#148; represents
the 53&nbsp;weeks ended February&nbsp;3, 2001 and &#147;fiscal 1999&#148; represents the 52&nbsp;weeks
ended January&nbsp;29, 2000.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>General</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc. (Barnes &#038; Noble or the Company), the nation&#146;s largest
bookseller<sup>1</sup>, as of February&nbsp;2, 2002 operates 896 bookstores and 1,038
video-game and entertainment-software stores. Of the 896 bookstores, 591
operate under the Barnes &#038; Noble Booksellers, Bookstop and Bookstar trade names
(40 of which were opened in fiscal 2001) and 305 operate under the B. Dalton
Bookseller, Doubleday Book Shops and Scribner&#146;s Bookstore trade names. Through
its approximate 36&nbsp;percent interest in barnesandnoble.com llc (Barnes &#038;
Noble.com), the Company is one of the largest sellers of books on the Internet.
The Company, through its acquisitions of Babbage&#146;s Etc. LLC (Babbage&#146;s Etc.)
and Funco, Inc. (now known as GameStop, Inc.), is the nation&#146;s largest
video-game and PC-entertainment software specialty retailer, operating 1,038
video-game and entertainment-software stores under the GameStop, Babbage&#146;s,
Software Etc. and FuncoLand trade names, a Web site, gamestop.com, and <I>Game
Informer</I>, one of the largest multi-platform video-game magazines, with
circulation of over 415,000 subscribers. The Company employed approximately
45,000 full- and part-time employees as of February&nbsp;2, 2002.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble is the nation&#146;s largest operator of bookstores<sup>1</sup> with 591
Barnes &#038; Noble bookstores located in 49 states and the District of Columbia as
of February&nbsp;2, 2002. With more than 35&nbsp;years of bookselling experience,
management has a strong sense of customers&#146; changing needs and the Company
leads book retailing with a &#147;community store&#148; concept. Barnes &#038; Noble&#146;s typical
bookstore offers a comprehensive title base, a caf&#233;, a children&#146;s section, a
music department, a magazine section and a calendar of ongoing events,
including author appearances and children&#146;s activities, that make each Barnes &#038;
Noble bookstore an active part of its community.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble bookstores range in size from 10,000 to 60,000 square feet
depending upon market size, and each store features an authoritative selection
of books, ranging from 60,000 to 200,000 titles. The comprehensive title
selection is diverse and reflects local interests. In addition, Barnes &#038; Noble
emphasizes books published by small and independent publishers and university
presses. Bestsellers represent only three percent of Barnes &#038; Noble bookstore
sales. Complementing this extensive on-site selection, all Barnes &#038; Noble
bookstores provide customers with access to the millions of books available to
online shoppers while offering an option to have the book sent to the store or
shipped directly to the customer. All Barnes &#038; Noble bookstores are equipped
with the BookMaster in-store operating system, which enhances the Company&#146;s
merchandise-replenishment system, resulting in higher in-stock positions and
better productivity at the store level through efficiencies in receiving,
cashiering and returns processing.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During fiscal 2001, the Company added 0.8&nbsp;million square feet to the
Barnes &#038; Noble bookstore base, bringing the total square footage to 14.2
million square feet, a six percent increase over the prior year. Barnes &#038; Noble
bookstores contributed approximately 90&nbsp;percent of the Company&#146;s total
bookstore sales in fiscal 2001. The Company plans to open between 40 and 45
Barnes &#038; Noble bookstores in fiscal
2002, which are expected to average 26,000 square feet in size.
</FONT>
<P>
<HR size="1" width="18%" align="left" noshade>

<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0">
<TR valign="top">
      <TD width="1%" align="left" nowrap><FONT size="2"><sup>1</sup></FONT></TD>
        <TD width="2%"><FONT size="2">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
        <TD width="97%"><FONT size="2"> Based upon sales reported in trade publications and public filings.</FONT></TD>
</TR>
</TABLE>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">5</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>




<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At the end of fiscal 2001, the Company operated 305 B. Dalton bookstores
in 45 states and the District of Columbia. B. Dalton bookstores employ
merchandising strategies that target the &#147;Middle American&#148; consumer book
market, offering a wide range of bestsellers and general-interest titles. Most
B. Dalton bookstores range in size from 2,000 to 6,000 square feet, and while
they are appropriate to the size of adjacent mall tenants, the opening of
superstores in nearby locations continues to have a significant adverse impact
on B. Dalton bookstores.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is continuing to execute a strategy to maximize returns from
its B. Dalton bookstores in response to declining sales attributable primarily
to superstore competition. Part of the Company&#146;s strategy has been to close
underperforming stores, which has resulted in the closing of between 35 and 90
B. Dalton bookstores per year since 1989.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In 1998, the Company and Bertelsmann AG (Bertelsmann) completed the
formation of a limited liability company to operate the online retail
bookselling operations of the Company&#146;s wholly owned subsidiary,
barnesandnoble.com inc. The new entity, barnesandnoble.com llc (Barnes &#038;
Noble.com), was formed by combining the online bookselling operations of the
Company with funds contributed by the international media company Bertelsmann,
one of the largest integrated media companies in the world. In 1999, Barnes &#038;
Noble.com Inc. completed an initial public offering (IPO)&nbsp;of 28.75&nbsp;million
shares of Class&nbsp;A Common Stock and used the proceeds to purchase a 20&nbsp;percent
interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. As a result, the Company and Bertelsmann each
retained a 40&nbsp;percent interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com from the date of the IPO
through November 2000. In November 2000, Barnes &#038; Noble.com acquired
Fatbrain.com, Inc. (Fatbrain), the third largest online bookseller. Barnes &#038;
Noble.com issued shares of its common stock to Fatbrain shareholders. As a
result of this merger, the Company and Bertelsmann each retained an approximate
36&nbsp;percent interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. Accordingly, the Company&#146;s share in
the net loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com was 40&nbsp;percent from the beginning of fiscal
2000 through November 2000 and approximately 36&nbsp;percent thereafter.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble.com is a leading online retailer of knowledge, information,
education and entertainment-related products. Since opening its online store
in March 1997, Barnes &#038; Noble.com has attracted more than 11.2&nbsp;million
customers in 228 countries. In addition to books, the Barnes &#038; Noble.com Web
site, www.bn.com, sells music, DVD/video and magazine subscriptions. Barnes &#038;
Noble.com&#146;s online bookstore includes the largest-in-stock selection of
in-print book titles with access to one million titles for immediate delivery
and supplemented by more than 20&nbsp;million listings from its nationwide network
of out-of-print, rare and used book dealers. Barnes &#038; Noble.com offers its
customers fast delivery, easy and secure ordering and rich editorial content.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;According to Jupiter Media Metrix, in January 2002, Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s
Web site was the fifth-most-trafficked shopping site and was among the top 50
largest Web properties on the Internet. Co-marketing agreements with major Web
portals such as AOL, Yahoo! and MSN as well as content sites have extended
Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s brand and increased consumer exposure to its site. Barnes
&#038; Noble.com has also established a network of remote storefronts across the
Internet by creating direct links with more than 512,000 affiliate Web sites.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble further differentiates its product offerings from those of
its competitors by publishing books under its own imprints for sale in its
retail stores and through Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s online book sales. With
publishing and distribution rights to nearly 4,000 titles, Barnes &#038; Noble Books
offers customers high quality books at exceptional values, while generating
attractive gross margins.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As a result of its acquisitions of Babbage&#146;s Etc. and Funco, Inc. in
October 1999 and June 2000, respectively, the Company is the nation&#146;s largest
video-game and PC-entertainment software specialty retailer. The Company owns
and operates 1,038 video-game and entertainment-software stores located in
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">6</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">49
states, Puerto Rico and Guam. The Company&#146;s video-game and
entertainment-software stores range in size from 500 to 5,000 square feet
(averaging 1,500 square feet) depending upon market demographics. Stores
feature video-game hardware and software, PC-entertainment software and a
multitude of accessories. The Company operates stores under the GameStop,
Babbage&#146;s, Software Etc. and FuncoLand trade names, a Web site, gamestop.com
and <I>Game Informer </I>magazine (collectively, GameStop or Video Game &#038;
Entertainment Software).
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Critical Accounting Policies</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Management&#146;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and Results of
Operations discusses the Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements, which
have been prepared in accordance with accounting principles generally accepted
in the United States. The preparation of these financial statements require
management to make estimates and assumptions in certain circumstances that
affect amounts reported in the accompanying consolidated financial statements
and related footnotes. In preparing these financial statements, management has
made its best estimates and judgments of certain amounts included in the
financial statements, giving due consideration to materiality. The Company does
not believe there is a great likelihood that materially different amounts would
be reported related to the accounting policies described below. However,
application of these accounting policies involves the exercise of judgment and
use of assumptions as to future uncertainties and, as a result, actual results
could differ from these estimates.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Impairment of Long-Lived Assets</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s long-lived assets include property and equipment and
intangibles (primarily goodwill). At February&nbsp;2, 2002, the Company had $595.8
million of property and equipment, net of accumulated depreciation and $352.9
million of goodwill, net of amortization, accounting for approximately 36.2% of
the Company&#146;s total assets. The Company periodically reviews its long-lived
assets for impairment whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that
their carrying amounts may not be recoverable or their depreciation or
amortization periods should be accelerated. The Company assesses
recoverability based on several factors, including management&#146;s intention with
respect to its stores and those stores&#146; projected undiscounted cash flows. An
impairment loss is recognized for the amount by which the carrying amount of
the assets exceeds the present value of their projected cash flows. For a
further discussion, see Newly Issued Accounting Pronouncements.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During fiscal 2000, the Company recorded a non-cash charge to operating
earnings of $106.8&nbsp;million. This charge included approximately $69.9&nbsp;million
of goodwill and $32.4&nbsp;million of property, plant and equipment related to the
book business, primarily goodwill associated with the purchase of B. Dalton and
other mall-bookstore assets.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Marketable Equity Securities</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All marketable equity securities are classified as available-for-sale.
The Company carries these
investments at fair value, based on quoted market prices, with unrealized gains
and losses (net of taxes) included in accumulated other comprehensive earnings,
which is reflected as a separate component of shareholders&#146; equity. Realized
gains and losses are recognized in the Company&#146;s consolidated statement of
operations when securities are sold or impairment is considered other than
temporary. The Company reviews its equity holdings on a regular basis to
evaluate whether or not each security has experienced an
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">7</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">other-than-temporary
decline in fair value. The Company has reviewed each of the companies&#146;
financial position, results of operations, stock price performance and various
analyst research reports and believes that the declines in fair value of its
equity holdings are temporary.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Closed Store Expenses</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon a formal decision to close or relocate a store, the Company charges
unrecoverable costs to expense. Such costs include the net book value of
abandoned fixtures and leasehold improvements and a provision for future lease
obligations, net of expected sublease recoveries. Costs associated with store
closings of $9.8&nbsp;million, $5.0&nbsp;million and $5.4&nbsp;million during fiscal 2001,
fiscal 2000 and fiscal 1999, respectively, are included in selling and
administrative expenses in the accompanying consolidated statements of
operations.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">8</FONT>

</CENTER>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>52 Weeks Ended February&nbsp;2, 2002 Compared with 53 Weeks Ended<BR>
February&nbsp;3, 2001</B>
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Sales</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s sales increased $494.6&nbsp;million or 11.3% during fiscal 2001
to $4.870&nbsp;billion from $4.376&nbsp;billion during fiscal 2000. Contributing to this
improvement was an increase of $363.8&nbsp;million from Video Game &#038; Entertainment
Software store sales. Fiscal 2001 sales from Barnes &#038; Noble bookstores, which
contributed 69.0% of total sales or 89.6% of total bookstore sales, increased
6.0% to $3.359&nbsp;billion from $3.170&nbsp;billion in fiscal 2000.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The increase in bookstore sales was primarily attributable to the 2.7%
growth in Barnes &#038; Noble comparable store sales and sales from the 40 new
Barnes &#038; Noble stores opened during fiscal 2001. This increase was partially
offset by declining sales of B. Dalton, due to 35 store closings and a
comparable store sales decline of (3.7%) in fiscal 2001.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;GameStop sales during fiscal 2001 increased to $1.121&nbsp;billion from $757.6
million during fiscal 2000. This increase in sales was primarily attributable
to the 32.0% growth in the GameStop comparable
store sales and sales from the 74 new GameStop stores opened during fiscal
2001. This increase was also
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">11</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">attributable to the inclusion of a full year of
Funco, Inc. sales in fiscal 2001 compared with sales for approximately one-half
of fiscal 2000.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Cost of Sales and Occupancy</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s cost of sales and occupancy includes costs such as rental
expense, common area maintenance, merchant association dues and lease-required
advertising.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of sales and occupancy increased $390.3&nbsp;million, or 12.3%, to $3.560
billion in fiscal 2001 from $3.170&nbsp;billion in fiscal 2000, primarily due to
growth in the Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software segment. The Company&#146;s gross
margin rate decreased to 26.9% in fiscal 2001 from 27.6% in fiscal 2000. This
decrease was primarily attributable to the lower gross margins in the Video
Game &#038; Entertainment Software segment and slightly lower gross margins in the
bookstore segment due to discounts related to the Readers&#146; Advantage&#153; program.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Selling and Administrative Expenses</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling and administrative expenses increased $91.3&nbsp;million, or 11.2%, to
$904.3&nbsp;million in fiscal 2001 from $813.0&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000, primarily due
to growth in the Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software segment and the increase
in bookstore expenses from the opening of 40 Barnes &#038; Noble stores in fiscal
2001. Selling and administrative expenses remained unchanged at 18.6% of sales
during fiscal 2001 and 2000.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Legal Settlement Expense</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2001, the Company recorded a pre-tax charge of $4.5&nbsp;million in
connection with a lawsuit brought by the American Booksellers Association and
26 independent bookstores. The charges included a settlement of $2.4&nbsp;million to
be paid to plaintiffs and approximately $2.1&nbsp;million in legal expenses incurred
by the Company during the first quarter.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Depreciation and amortization increased $3.1&nbsp;million, or 2.1%, to $147.8
million in fiscal 2001 from $144.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000. The increase was
primarily the result of the increase in depreciation and amortization in the
Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software segment offset by the reduction in
depreciable assets in our mall bookstores due to the impairment charge recorded
in fiscal 2000.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Pre-Opening Expenses</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Pre-opening expenses increased in fiscal 2001 to $8.0&nbsp;million from $7.7
million in fiscal 2000. Due to management&#146;s expense control efforts,
pre-opening expenses increased only slightly while opening 40 Barnes &#038; Noble
stores and 74 new GameStop stores in fiscal 2001, compared with 32 new Barnes &#038;
Noble stores and 65 new GameStop stores during fiscal 2000.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Operating Profit</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Operating profit increased to $245.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 2001 from $133.8
million in fiscal 2000. Operating profit increased $9.6&nbsp;million to $250.3
million, before the effect of the $4.5&nbsp;million legal
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">12</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">settlement expense during
fiscal 2001, from $240.7&nbsp;million, before the effect of the $106.8&nbsp;million
impairment charge during fiscal 2000. Bookstore operating profit decreased
7.9% to $216.2&nbsp;million, before the effect of the $4.5&nbsp;million legal settlement
expense, from $234.6&nbsp;million, before the effect of the $106.8&nbsp;million
impairment charge, primarily attributable to lower comparable store sales and
lower gross margins due to discounts related to the Readers&#146; Advantage&#153;
program. Bookstore operating margin decreased to 5.8% of sales during fiscal
2001, before the effect of the legal settlement expense, from 6.5% of sales
during fiscal 2000, before the effect of the impairment charge.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Interest Expense, Net and Amortization of Deferred Financing Fees</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Interest expense, net of interest income, and amortization of deferred
financing fees, decreased $17.2&nbsp;million to $36.3&nbsp;million in fiscal 2001 from
$53.5&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000. The decrease was primarily the result of reduced
borrowings due to effective working capital management and lower interest rates
on the Company&#146;s outstanding debt, partially through the issuance of the
Company&#146;s convertible subordinated notes sold in March 2001.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Equity in Net Loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In November 2000, Barnes &#038; Noble.com acquired Fatbrain.com, Inc.
(Fatbrain), the third largest online bookseller. Barnes &#038; Noble.com issued
shares of its common stock to Fatbrain shareholders. As a result of this
merger, the Company and Bertelsmann each retained an approximate 36&nbsp;percent
interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. Accordingly, the Company&#146;s share in the net
loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com is based on an approximate 40&nbsp;percent equity
interest from the beginning of fiscal 2000 through November 2000 and
approximately 36&nbsp;percent thereafter. The Company&#146;s equity in the net loss of
Barnes &#038; Noble.com for fiscal 2001 and fiscal 2000 was $88.4&nbsp;million and $103.9
million, respectively.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Other Expense</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Other expense of $11.7&nbsp;million in fiscal 2001 was due to $4.0&nbsp;million in
equity losses in iUniverse.com, $2.5&nbsp;million in equity losses in <I>BOOK&#174; </I>magazine
and $5.5&nbsp;million in equity losses in enews, inc., partially offset by a
one-time gain of $0.3&nbsp;million from the partial sale of Indigo Books &#038; Music
Inc. (formerly Chapters Inc.). Other expense of $9.3&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000
was primarily due to the equity losses of iUniverse.com, partially offset by a
one-time gain of $0.3&nbsp;million from the partial sale of iUniverse.com.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Provision for Income Taxes</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble&#146;s effective tax rate in fiscal 2001 decreased to 41.5
percent compared with (57.5) percent during fiscal 2000. The fiscal 2001
decrease was primarily related to the goodwill write-down associated with the
impairment charge, which provided no tax benefit in fiscal 2000.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">13</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Earnings (Loss)</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As a result of the factors discussed above, the Company reported
consolidated net earnings of $64.0&nbsp;million (or $0.94 per share) during fiscal
2001 compared with a net loss of ($52.0) million (or ($0.81) per share) during
fiscal 2000. Components of diluted earnings per share are as follows:

</CENTER>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>53 Weeks Ended February&nbsp;3, 2001 Compared with 52 Weeks Ended<BR>
January&nbsp;29, 2000</B>
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Sales</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s sales increased $889.8&nbsp;million or 25.5% during fiscal 2000
to $4.376&nbsp;billion from $3.486&nbsp;billion during fiscal 1999. Contributing to this
improvement was an increase of $533.8&nbsp;million attributable to the inclusion of
sales from Babbage&#146;s Etc. and Funco, Inc. (Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software
or GameStop). Through its acquisitions of Babbage&#146;s Etc. in October 1999 and
Funco, Inc. in June 2000 (the Acquisitions), the Company has become the
nation&#146;s largest video-game and PC-entertainment software specialty retailer.
Fiscal 2000 sales from Barnes &#038; Noble bookstores, which contributed 72.4% of
total sales or 87.6% of total bookstore sales, increased 12.3% to $3.170
billion from $2.822&nbsp;billion in fiscal 1999.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The increase in bookstore sales was primarily attributable to the 4.9%
growth in Barnes &#038; Noble comparable store sales and the opening of 32 Barnes &#038;
Noble stores during fiscal 2000. This increase was partially offset by
declining sales of B. Dalton, due to 61 store closings and a comparable store
sales decline of (1.7%) in fiscal 2000.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;GameStop sales during fiscal 2000 increased to $757.6&nbsp;million from $223.7
million during fiscal 1999. This increase in sales was attributable to the
inclusion of a full year of Babbage&#146;s Etc.&#146;s sales in
fiscal 2000 compared with sales for the fourth quarter only in fiscal
1999, as well as the inclusion of Funco, Inc. sales for approximately one-half
of fiscal 2000. Comparable store sales as if Babbage&#146;s Etc.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">14</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">and Funco, Inc.
had been included for the entire 52-week period decreased 6.7%.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Cost of Sales and Occupancy</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s cost of sales and occupancy includes costs such as rental
expense, common area maintenance, merchant association dues and lease-required
advertising.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cost of sales and occupancy increased to $3.170&nbsp;billion in fiscal 2000
from $2.484&nbsp;billion in fiscal 1999 primarily due to the increase in Video Game
&#038; Entertainment Software&#146;s cost of sales and occupancy as a result of the
Acquisitions. The Company&#146;s gross margin rate decreased to 27.6% in fiscal 2000
from 28.8% in fiscal 1999. This decrease was primarily attributable to lower
gross margins in the Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software stores, partially
offset by improved leverage on occupancy costs as well as a favorable product
mix in the bookstores.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Selling and Administrative Expenses</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Selling and administrative expenses increased $161.9&nbsp;million, or 24.9%, to
$813.0&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000 from $651.1&nbsp;million in fiscal 1999 primarily due
to the increase in Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software&#146;s selling and
administrative expenses as a result of the Acquisitions. Selling and
administrative expenses decreased slightly to 18.6% of sales during fiscal 2000
from 18.7% during fiscal 1999.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Depreciation and Amortization</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Depreciation and amortization increased $32.5&nbsp;million, or 28.9%, to $144.8
million in fiscal 2000 from $112.3&nbsp;million in fiscal 1999. The increase was
primarily the result of the increase in GameStop&#146;s depreciation and
amortization as a result of the Acquisitions, as well as depreciation related
to the Barnes &#038; Noble stores opened during fiscal 2000 and fiscal 1999.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Pre-Opening Expenses</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Pre-opening expenses increased in fiscal 2000 to $7.7&nbsp;million from $6.8
million in fiscal 1999. This increase was the result of additional labor used
to facilitate the rollout of the new Barnes &#038; Noble bookstores as well as the
opening of 65 new GameStop stores.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Impairment Charge</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During fiscal 2000, the Company recorded a non-cash charge to operating
earnings of $106.8&nbsp;million ($92.4&nbsp;million after taxes or $1.44 per share).
This charge included approximately $69.9&nbsp;million of goodwill and $32.4&nbsp;million
of property, plant and equipment related to the book business, primarily
goodwill associated with the purchase of B. Dalton, other mall-bookstore assets
and $6.2&nbsp;million of warehouse equipment. The Company&#146;s mall-based bookstores
have experienced significant declines in sales and profitability as a result of
increased competition from book superstores and Internet book retailers. In
fiscal 2000, B. Dalton comparable store sales declined (1.7%) compared with an
increase in comparable store sales of 0.1% in fiscal 1999. As a result, the
anticipated future cash flows from certain stores were no longer sufficient to
recover the carrying value of the underlying assets. Also, included in this
charge were other charges of $4.5&nbsp;million related to the write-off of certain
investments which had continuing adverse financial results.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Operating Profit</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Operating profit decreased to $133.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000 from $232.1
million in fiscal 1999.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">15</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">Operating profit, before the effect of the $106.8
million impairment charge, increased $8.5&nbsp;million to $240.7&nbsp;million during
fiscal 2000. Bookstore operating profit, before the effect of the $106.8
million impairment charge, increased 8.3% to $234.6&nbsp;million. Bookstore
operating margin, before the effect of the impairment charge, decreased
slightly to 6.5% of sales during fiscal 2000 from 6.6% of sales in fiscal 1999
as a result of the inclusion of Calendar Club operating results.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Interest Expense, Net and Amortization of Deferred Financing Fees</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Interest expense, net of interest income, and amortization of deferred
financing fees, increased $29.7&nbsp;million to $53.5&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000 from
$23.8&nbsp;million in fiscal 1999. This increase was primarily the result of the
increased borrowings under the Company&#146;s revolving credit facility used to
support the Company&#146;s Acquisitions and the common stock repurchase program.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Equity in Net Loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As a result of the Barnes &#038; Noble.com Inc. IPO on May&nbsp;25, 1999, the
Company and Bertelsmann each retained a 40&nbsp;percent interest in Barnes &#038;
Noble.com. Accordingly, the Company&#146;s share in the net loss of Barnes &#038;
Noble.com for fiscal 1999 was based on a 50&nbsp;percent equity interest from the
beginning of fiscal 1999 through May&nbsp;25, 1999 and 40&nbsp;percent through the end of
1999. The Company&#146;s equity in the net loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com for fiscal
1999 was $42.0&nbsp;million. In November 2000, Barnes &#038; Noble.com acquired
Fatbrain.com, Inc. (Fatbrain), the third largest online bookseller. Barnes &#038;
Noble.com issued shares of its common stock to Fatbrain shareholders. As a
result of this merger, the Company and Bertelsmann each retained an approximate
36&nbsp;percent interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. Accordingly, the Company&#146;s share in
the net losses of Barnes &#038; Noble.com for fiscal 2000 was based on an
approximate 40&nbsp;percent equity interest from the beginning of fiscal 2000
through November 2000 and approximately 36&nbsp;percent thereafter. The Company&#146;s
equity in the net loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com for fiscal 2000 was $103.9
million.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Gain on Formation of Barnes &#038; Noble.com</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under the terms of the November&nbsp;12, 1998 joint venture agreement between
the Company and Bertelsmann, the Company received a $25.0&nbsp;million payment from
Bertelsmann in fiscal 1999 in connection with the Barnes &#038; Noble.com Inc. IPO.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Other Income (Expense)</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Other expense of ($9.3) million in fiscal 2000 was primarily due to the
equity losses of iUniverse.com. Other income of $27.4&nbsp;million in fiscal 1999
was primarily attributable to a one-time gain of $11.0&nbsp;million on the partial
sale of Indigo Books &#038; Music Inc., a one-time gain of $22.4&nbsp;million in
connection with the sale of its investment in NuvoMedia Inc. (NuvoMedia) to
Gemstar International Ltd., partially offset by a one-time charge of ($5.0)
million attributable to the termination of the planned Ingram Book Group
(Ingram) acquisition.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Provision for Income Taxes</I>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble&#146;s effective tax rate in fiscal 2000 increased to (57.5)
percent compared with 41.0&nbsp;percent during fiscal 1999. The fiscal 2000
increase was primarily related to the goodwill write-down associated with the
impairment charge, which provided no tax benefit.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><I>Earnings (Loss)</I>
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">16</FONT>

The Company&#146;s earnings, before the effect of the impairment charge, were $40.5
million during fiscal 2000 compared with $124.5&nbsp;million during fiscal 1999.
