<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Seasonality</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s business, like that of many retailers, is seasonal, with the
major portion of sales and operating profit realized during the quarter which
includes the holiday selling season. The Company has now reported operating
profit for 23 consecutive quarters.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Liquidity and Capital Resources</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Working capital requirements are generally at their highest during the
Company&#146;s fiscal quarter ending on or about January&nbsp;31 due to the higher
payments to vendors for holiday season merchandise purchases and the
replenishment of merchandise inventories following this period of increased
sales. In addition, the Company&#146;s sales and merchandise inventory levels will
fluctuate from quarter to quarter as a result of the number and timing of new
store openings, as well as the amount and timing of sales contributed by new
stores.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash flows from operating activities, funds available under its revolving
credit facility and vendor
financing continue to provide the Company with liquidity and capital resources
for store expansion, seasonal working capital requirements and capital
investments.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Cash Flow</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Cash flows provided from operating activities were $457.4&nbsp;million, $80.5
million and $187.3&nbsp;million during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. In
fiscal 2001, the increase in cash flows from
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">17</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">operating activities was primarily
attributable to increased accounts payable leverage and improvement in net
earnings. In fiscal 2000, the decrease in cash flows from operating activities
was primarily attributable to a weaker-than-expected holiday season which
resulted in lower net earnings and an increase in standing inventory as well as
an increase in prepaid rent due to the fiscal year-end date. In fiscal 1999,
the improvement in cash flows was primarily due to the improvement in net
earnings.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Retail earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation and amortization
(EBITDA)&nbsp;increased $10.8&nbsp;million or 2.8% to $392.2&nbsp;million in fiscal 2001 from
$381.4&nbsp;million in fiscal 2000. This improvement in EBITDA is due to the growth
in the Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software segment and the continuing
maturation of the Barnes &#038; Noble stores offset by the lower gross margins in
the bookstore segment due to the increased spending by Readers&#146; Advantage&#153;
members. Total debt to retail EBITDA improved to 1.14 times in fiscal 2001
from 1.75 times in fiscal 2000 primarily due to increased cash flows from
operations that reduced debt incurred to fund the Company&#146;s Acquisitions. The
weighted-average age per square foot of the Company&#146;s 591 Barnes &#038; Noble stores
was 5.3&nbsp;years as of February&nbsp;2, 2002 and is expected to increase to
approximately 5.8&nbsp;years by February&nbsp;1, 2003. As the relatively young Barnes &#038;
Noble stores mature, and as the number of new stores opened during the fiscal
year decreases as a percentage of the existing store base, the increasing
operating profits of Barnes &#038; Noble stores are expected to generate a greater
portion of cash flows required for working capital, including new store
inventories, capital expenditures and other initiatives. Additionally, due to
the Barnes &#038; Noble.com Inc. IPO in fiscal 1999, retail cash flows are fully
available to support the Company&#146;s working capital requirements.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Capital Structure</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Strong cash flows from operations and a continued emphasis on working
capital management strengthened the Company&#146;s balance sheet in fiscal 2001.
Shareholders&#146; equity increased 14.2% to $888.1&nbsp;million as of February&nbsp;2, 2002,
from $777.7&nbsp;million as of February&nbsp;3, 2001.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company has an $850.0&nbsp;million senior credit facility (the Facility),
obtained in November 1997, with a syndicate led by The Chase Manhattan Bank.
The Facility is structured as a five-year revolving credit. The Facility
permits borrowings at various interest-rate options based on the prime rate or
London Interbank Offer Rate (LIBOR)&nbsp;depending upon certain financial tests. In
addition, the agreement requires the Company to pay a commitment fee up to 0.25
percent of the unused portion depending upon certain financial tests. The
Facility contains covenants, limitations and events of default typical of
credit facilities of this size and nature.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The amount outstanding under the Facility has been classified as long-term
debt in the accompanying consolidated balance sheets due to both the Company&#146;s
intent and ability to maintain principal amounts.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2000, the Company obtained an additional $100.0&nbsp;million senior
unsecured seasonal credit facility (seasonal credit facility) with a syndicate
of banks led by The Chase Manhattan Bank. The seasonal credit facility, which
matured on January&nbsp;31, 2001, permitted for borrowings at an interest rate
based on LIBOR. In addition, the agreement required the Company to pay a
commitment fee of 0.375&nbsp;percent of the unused portion. The seasonal credit
facility was guaranteed by all restricted subsidiaries of Barnes &#038; Noble.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2001, the Company issued $300.0&nbsp;million, 5.25&nbsp;percent
convertible subordinated notes due March&nbsp;15, 2009, further strengthening its
balance sheet. The notes are convertible into the Company&#146;s common stock at a
conversion price of $32.512 per share.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Borrowings under the Company&#146;s senior and seasonal credit facilities
averaged $689.3&nbsp;million,
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">18</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">$697.8&nbsp;million and $397.1&nbsp;million and peaked at $870.0
million, $918.7&nbsp;million and $693.5&nbsp;million during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999,
respectively. The ratio of debt to equity improved significantly to 0.51:1.00
as of February&nbsp;2, 2002 from 0.86:1.00 as of February&nbsp;3, 2001, primarily due to
decreased borrowings under the Company&#146;s senior credit facility.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Interest rate swap agreements are valued based on market quotes obtained
from dealers. The estimated fair value of the interest rate swaps liability was
$2.3&nbsp;million and $0.5&nbsp;million at February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001,
respectively. The interest rate swaps are included as a component of other
long-term liabilities.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Capital Investment</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Capital expenditures totaled $168.8&nbsp;million, $134.3&nbsp;million and $146.3
million during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. Capital expenditures
in fiscal 2002, primarily for the opening of between 40 and 45 new Barnes &#038;
Noble stores and 175 GameStop stores, are expected to be between $170&nbsp;million
and $190&nbsp;million, although commitment to such expenditures has not yet been
made.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Based on current operating levels and the store expansion planned for the
next fiscal year, management believes cash flows generated from operating
activities, short-term vendor financing and borrowing capacity under its
revolving credit facility will be sufficient to meet the Company&#146;s working
capital and debt service requirements, and support the development of its
short- and long-term strategies for at least the next 12&nbsp;months.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 1999, the Board of Directors authorized a common stock
repurchase program for the purchase of up to $250.0&nbsp;million of the Company&#146;s
common shares. As of February&nbsp;3, 2001, the Company has repurchased 5,504,700
shares at a cost of approximately $117.4&nbsp;million under this program. The
repurchased shares are held in treasury.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Barnes &#038; Noble.com</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On November&nbsp;12, 1998, the Company and Bertelsmann completed the formation
of a joint venture to operate the online retail bookselling operations of the
Company&#146;s wholly owned subsidiary, Barnes &#038; Noble.com Inc. The new entity,
Barnes &#038; Noble.com, was structured as a limited liability company. Under the
terms of the relevant agreements, effective as of October&nbsp;31, 1998, the Company
and Bertelsmann each retained a 50&nbsp;percent membership interest in Barnes &#038;
Noble.com. The Company contributed substantially all of the assets and
liabilities of its online operations to the joint venture and Bertelsmann paid
$75.0&nbsp;million to the Company and made a $150.0&nbsp;million cash contribution to the
joint venture. Bertelsmann also agreed to contribute an additional $50.0
million to the joint venture for future working capital requirements. The
Company recognized a pre-tax gain during fiscal 1998 in the amount of $126.4
million, of which $63.8&nbsp;million was recognized in earnings based on the $75.0
million received directly and $62.7&nbsp;million ($36.4&nbsp;million after taxes) was
reflected in additional paid-in capital based on
the Company&#146;s share of the incremental equity of the joint venture
resulting from the $150.0&nbsp;million Bertelsmann contribution.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On May&nbsp;25, 1999, Barnes &#038; Noble.com Inc. completed an IPO of 28.75&nbsp;million
shares of Class&nbsp;A Common Stock and used the proceeds to purchase a 20&nbsp;percent
interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. As a result, the Company and Bertelsmann each
retained a 40&nbsp;percent interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. The Company recorded an
increase in additional paid-in capital of $200.3&nbsp;million ($116.2&nbsp;million after
taxes) representing the Company&#146;s incremental share in the equity of Barnes &#038;
Noble.com.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under the terms of the November&nbsp;12, 1998 joint venture agreement between
the Company and Bertelsmann, the Company received a $25.0&nbsp;million payment from
Bertelsmann in connection with the
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">19</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">IPO.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The accompanying consolidated financial statements, in accordance with the
equity method of accounting, reflect the Company&#146;s investment in Barnes &#038;
Noble.com as a single line item in the consolidated balance sheets as of
February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001 and reflect the Company&#146;s share of the
net loss of Barnes &#038; Noble.com as a single line item in the consolidated
statements of operations for fiscal years 2001, 2000 and 1999.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Certain Relationships and Related Transactions</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company believes that the transactions and agreements discussed below
(including renewals of any existing agreements) between the Company and its
affiliates are at least as favorable to the Company as could be obtained from
unaffiliated parties. The Board of Directors and the Audit Committee must
approve in advance any proposed transaction or agreement with affiliates and
will utilize procedures in evaluating the terms and provisions of such proposed
transaction or agreement as are appropriate in light of the fiduciary duties of
directors under Delaware law.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company leases space for its executive offices in properties in which
Leonard Riggio, Chairman of the Board and principal stockholder of Barnes &#038;
Noble, has a minority interest. The space was rented at an aggregate annual
rent including real estate taxes of approximately $4.0&nbsp;million, $3.4&nbsp;million
and $2.9&nbsp;million in fiscal years 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. Rent per
square foot is approximately $28, which is below market.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company leases a 75,000-square-foot office/warehouse from a
partnership in which Leonard Riggio has a 50&nbsp;percent interest, pursuant to a
lease expiring in 2023. Pursuant to such lease, the Company paid $0.5&nbsp;million,
$0.6&nbsp;million and $0.6&nbsp;million in fiscal years 2001, 2000 and 1999,
respectively.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company leases retail space in a building in which Barnes &#038; Noble
College Bookstores, Inc. (B&#038;N College), a company owned by Leonard Riggio,
subleases space for its executive offices from the Company. Occupancy costs
allocated by the Company to B&#038;N College for this space totaled $0.7&nbsp;million<B>,</B>
$0.7&nbsp;million and $0.7&nbsp;million for fiscal years 2001, 2000 and 1999,
respectively. The amount paid by B&#038;N College to the Company approximates the
cost per square foot paid by the Company to its unaffiliated third-party
landlord.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company subleases warehouse space from Barnes &#038; Noble.com in Reno,
Nevada. The Company paid Barnes &#038; Noble.com $1.8&nbsp;million and $1.4&nbsp;million for
such subleased space during fiscal 2001 and 2000, respectively. Additionally,
in January 2001, the Company purchased $6.2&nbsp;million of
warehouse equipment (valued at original cost) from Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s
Reno warehouse. Barnes &#038; Noble.com recently determined it could not
effectively utilize the full capacity of the Reno, Nevada distribution center.
As a result, Barnes &#038; Noble.com&#146;s Board of Directors approved the transfer of
the Reno warehouse lease and the sale of inventory located in Reno to the
Company. The Company purchased the inventory from Barnes &#038; Noble.com at cost
for approximately $10.0&nbsp;million. In addition, the Company intends to spend
approximately $2.0&nbsp;million to refurbish the facility. The Company&#146;s Board of
Directors also approved the Company&#146;s assumption of the lease, which expires in
2010, and the hiring of all of the employees at the Reno facility. The Company
intends to use the Reno facility to facilitate distribution to its current and
future West Coast stores. In connection with the transition, Barnes &#038; Noble.com
will pay rent for the Reno facility through December&nbsp;31, 2002 of $1.6&nbsp;million.
The Reno lease assignment and the transfer the Reno facility to the Company is
expected to be completed during the first half of fiscal 2002.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">20</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company subleases to Barnes &#038; Noble.com approximately one-third of a
300,000-square-foot warehouse facility located in New Jersey. The Company has
received from Barnes &#038; Noble.com $0.5&nbsp;million annually for such subleased space
during each of the fiscal years 2001, 2000 and 1999. The amount paid by Barnes
&#038; Noble.com to the Company approximates the cost per square foot paid by the
Company as a tenant pursuant to the lease of the space from an unaffiliated
third party.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company has entered into an agreement (the Supply Agreement) with
Barnes &#038; Noble.com whereby the Company charges Barnes &#038; Noble.com the costs
associated with such purchases plus incremental overhead incurred by the
Company in connection with providing such inventory. The Supply Agreement is
subject to certain termination provisions. Barnes &#038; Noble.com purchased $119.3
million, $110.5&nbsp;million and $74.7&nbsp;million of merchandise from the Company
during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively, and Barnes &#038; Noble.com expects
to source purchases through the Company in the future.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company has entered into agreements whereby Barnes &#038; Noble.com
receives various services from the Company, including, among others, services
for payroll processing, benefits administration, insurance (property and
casualty, medical, dental and life), tax, traffic, fulfillment and
telecommunications. In accordance with the terms of such agreements the
Company has received, and expects to continue to receive, fees in an amount
equal to the direct costs plus incremental expenses associated with providing
such services. The Company received $5.5&nbsp;million, $1.7&nbsp;million and $2.0
million for such services during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The aggregate receivable from Barnes &#038; Noble.com in connection with the
agreements described above was $47.2&nbsp;million and $18.0&nbsp;million as of February
2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001, respectively.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company and Barnes &#038; Noble.com commenced a marketing program in
November 2000, whereby a customer purchases a &#147;Readers&#146; Advantage&#153; card&#148; for an
annual fee of $25.00. With this card, customers can receive discounts of 10
percent on all Company purchases and 5&nbsp;percent on all Barnes &#038; Noble.com
purchases. The Company and Barnes &#038; Noble.com have agreed to share the
expenses, net of revenue from the sale of the cards, related to this program in
proportion to the discounts customers receive on purchases with each company.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble.com, through its fulfillment centers, ships various
customer orders for the Company to its retail stores as well as to the
Company&#146;s customers&#146; homes. Barnes &#038; Noble.com charges the Company the costs
associated with such shipments plus any incremental overhead incurred by Barnes
&#038; Noble.com to process these orders. The Company paid Barnes &#038; Noble.com $1.0
million and $0.2&nbsp;million for shipping and handling during fiscal 2001 and 2000,
respectively. In addition, during
fiscal 2001, the Company and Barnes &#038; Noble.com reached an agreement
whereby the Company pays a commission on all items ordered by customers at the
Company&#146;s stores and shipped directly to customers&#146; homes by Barnes &#038;
Noble.com. Commissions paid for these sales were $0.4&nbsp;million during fiscal
2001.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company paid B&#038;N College certain operating costs B&#038;N College incurred
on the Company&#146;s behalf. These charges are included in the accompanying
consolidated statements of operations and approximated $0.2&nbsp;million, $0.3
million and $0.2&nbsp;million for fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. B&#038;N
College purchased $41.5&nbsp;million, $17.2&nbsp;million and $16.1&nbsp;million of merchandise
from the Company during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. The Company
charged B&#038;N College $1.5&nbsp;million, $1.3&nbsp;million and $1.0&nbsp;million for fiscal
years 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively, for capital expenditures, business
insurance and other operating costs incurred on its behalf.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company uses a jet aircraft owned by B&#038;N College and pays for the
costs and expenses of operating the aircraft based upon the Company&#146;s usage.
Such costs which include fuel, insurance, personnel and other costs,
approximated $2.2&nbsp;million, $2.4&nbsp;million and $2.2&nbsp;million during fiscal 2001,
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">21</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">2000 and 1999, respectively, and are included in the accompanying consolidated
statements of operations.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 1999, the Company acquired Babbage&#146;s Etc., one of the nation&#146;s
largest video-game and entertainment-software specialty retailers, a company
majority owned by Leonard Riggio, for $208.7&nbsp;million. An independent Special
Committee of the Board of Directors negotiated and approved the acquisition on
behalf of the Company. The Company made an additional payment of $9.7&nbsp;million
in 2002 due to certain financial performance targets having been met during
fiscal year 2001.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company is provided with national freight distribution, including
trucking, services by the LTA Group, Inc. (LTA), a company in which a brother
of Leonard Riggio owns a 20&nbsp;percent interest. The Company paid LTA $17.7
million, $16.7&nbsp;million and $13.1&nbsp;million for such services during fiscal years
2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. The Company believes the cost of freight
delivered to the stores compares favorably to the prices charged by publishers
and other third-party freight distributors.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Since 1993, the Company has used AEC One Stop Group, Inc. (AEC)&nbsp;as its
primary music and video supplier and to provide a music and video database.
AEC is one of the largest wholesale distributors of music and videos in the
United States. In 1999, AEC&#146;s parent corporation was acquired by an investor
group in which Leonard Riggio was a minority investor. The Company paid AEC
$168.1&nbsp;million, $159.2&nbsp;million and $126.2&nbsp;million for merchandise purchased
during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively. Amounts payable to AEC for
merchandise purchased were $51.1&nbsp;million and $39.4&nbsp;million as of February&nbsp;2,
2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001, respectively.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Newly Issued Accounting Pronouncements</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In June 2001, the Financial Accounting Standards Board (FASB)&nbsp;issued SFAS
No.&nbsp;141, &#147;Business Combinations&#148; and SFAS No.&nbsp;142, &#147;Goodwill and Other
Intangible Assets&#148;. SFAS No.&nbsp;141 requires the use of the purchase method of
accounting and prohibits the use of the pooling-of-interests method of
accounting for business combinations initiated after June&nbsp;30, 2001. SFAS No.
141 also requires that the Company recognize acquired intangible assets apart
from goodwill if the acquired intangible assets meet certain criteria. SFAS No.
141 applies to all business combinations initiated after June&nbsp;30, 2001 and for
purchase business combinations completed on or after July&nbsp;1, 2001. It also
requires that, upon adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;142, the Company reclassify the
carrying amounts of intangible assets and goodwill based
on the criteria in SFAS No.&nbsp;141.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;SFAS No.&nbsp;142 requires, among other things, that the Company no longer
amortize goodwill, but instead test goodwill for impairment at least annually.
In addition, SFAS No.&nbsp;142 requires that the Company identify reporting units
for the purposes of assessing potential future impairments of goodwill,
reassess the useful lives of other existing recognized intangible assets, and
cease amortization of intangible assets with an indefinite useful life. An
intangible asset with an indefinite useful life should be tested for impairment
in accordance with the guidance in SFAS No.&nbsp;142.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company will apply the new standards on accounting for goodwill and
other intangible assets beginning in the first quarter of the Company&#146;s fiscal
year ending February&nbsp;1, 2003, at which time the Company will cease to record
amortization expense on its goodwill. The adoption of SFAS No.&nbsp;142 will result
in an approximate $12.3&nbsp;million reduction of amortization expense in 2002. The
Company expects to complete its analysis of any potential impairment of
goodwill as a result of adopting this standard by the end of the second quarter
of fiscal 2002.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In August 2001, the FASB issued SFAS No.&nbsp;144, &#147;Accounting for the
Impairment or Disposal of Long-Lived Assets&#148;, that is applicable to financial
statements issued for fiscal years beginning after December&nbsp;15, 2001. The
FASB&#146;s new rules on asset impairment supersede SFAS No.&nbsp;121, &#147;Accounting
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">22</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P><FONT size="2">for
the Impairment of Long-Lived Assets and for Long-Lived Assets to be Disposed
Of&#148;, and portions of Accounting Principles Bulletin Opinion 30, &#147;Reporting the
Results of Operations&#148;. This new standard provides a single accounting model
for long-lived assets to be disposed of and significantly changes the criteria
that would have to be met to classify an asset as held-for-sale.
Classification as held-for-sale is an important distinction since such assets
are not depreciated and are stated at the lower of fair value and carrying
amount. This new standard also requires expected future operating losses from
discontinued operations to be displayed in the period(s) in which the losses
are incurred, rather than as of the measurement date as presently required.
The Company is currently evaluating the impact of this pronouncement to
determine its effect, if any, on the Company&#146;s financial position or operating
results.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>Recent Events</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On February&nbsp;19, 2002, the Company successfully completed an initial public
offering for its GameStop subsidiary, raising $250.0&nbsp;million in cash for the
Company and $98.0&nbsp;million in net proceeds for GameStop. Barnes &#038; Noble has
retained an approximate 63&nbsp;percent interest in GameStop.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the first quarter of 2002, the Board of Directors of Barnes &#038;
Noble.com approved the transfer of the Reno facility to the Company and the
Board of Directors of the Company approved the Company&#146;s assumption of the Reno
lease, the purchase of inventory, and the hiring of all the Reno employees. The
Reno lease assignment and the transfer of the operations of the Reno facility
to the Company is expected to be completed during the first half of 2002.
</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">(Thousands of dollars, except per share data)
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">For the 52&nbsp;weeks ended February&nbsp;2, 2002 (fiscal 2001), 53&nbsp;weeks ended February
3, 2001 (fiscal 2000) and 52&nbsp;weeks ended January&nbsp;29, 2000 (fiscal 1999).
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>1. Summary of Significant Accounting Policies</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2"><I>Business</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barnes &#038; Noble, Inc. (Barnes &#038; Noble), through its subsidiaries
(collectively, the Company), is primarily engaged in the sale of books, video
games and entertainment-software products. The Company employs two principal
bookselling strategies: its superstore strategy through its wholly owned
subsidiary Barnes &#038; Noble Booksellers, Inc., under its Barnes &#038; Noble
Booksellers, Bookstop and Bookstar trade names (hereafter collectively referred
to as Barnes &#038; Noble stores) and its mall strategy through its wholly owned
subsidiaries B. Dalton Bookseller, Inc. and Doubleday Book Shops, Inc., under
its B. Dalton stores, Doubleday Book Shops and Scribner&#146;s Bookstore trade names
(hereafter collectively referred to as B. Dalton stores). The Company is also
engaged in the online retailing of books and other products through an
approximate 36&nbsp;percent interest in barnesandnoble.com llc (Barnes &#038; Noble.com),
as more fully described in Note 8. The Company, through its acquisitions of
Babbage&#146;s Etc. LLC (Babbage&#146;s Etc.) and Funco, Inc. (now known as GameStop,
Inc.) operates video-game and entertainment-software stores under the GameStop,
Babbage&#146;s, Software Etc. and FuncoLand trade names, a Web site (gamestop.com)
and <I>Game Informer </I>magazine (hereafter collectively referred to as GameStop
stores). Additionally, the Company owns an approximate 74&nbsp;percent interest in
Calendar Club L.L.C. (Calendar Club), an operator of seasonal calendar kiosks.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Consolidation</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Barnes &#038;
Noble and its wholly and majority-owned subsidiaries. Investments in
affiliates in which ownership interests range from 20&nbsp;percent to 50&nbsp;percent,
principally Barnes &#038; Noble.com, are accounted for under the equity method. All
significant intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated in
consolidation.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Use of Estimates</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In preparing financial statements in conformity with generally accepted
accounting principles, the Company is required to make estimates and
assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and the
disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial
statements and revenues and expenses during the reporting period. Actual
results could differ from those estimates.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Cash and Cash Equivalents</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company considers all short-term, highly liquid instruments purchased
with an original maturity of three months or less to be cash equivalents.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">28</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS CONTINUED</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2"><I>Merchandise Inventories</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Merchandise inventories are stated at the lower of cost or market. Cost
is determined primarily by the retail inventory method on the first-in,
first-out (FIFO)&nbsp;basis for 81&nbsp;percent and 82&nbsp;percent of the Company&#146;s
merchandise inventories as of February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001,
respectively. Merchandise inventories of GameStop stores and Calendar Club
represent 11&nbsp;percent and 9&nbsp;percent of merchandise inventories as of February&nbsp;2,
2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001, respectively and are recorded based on the average
cost method. The remaining merchandise inventories are valued on the last-in,
first-out (LIFO)&nbsp;method.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;If substantially all of the merchandise inventories currently valued at
LIFO costs were valued at current costs, merchandise inventories would remain
unchanged as of February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Property and Equipment</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Property and equipment are carried at cost, less accumulated depreciation
and amortization. For financial reporting purposes, depreciation is computed
using the straight-line method over estimated useful lives. For tax purposes,
different methods are used. Maintenance and repairs are expensed as incurred,
while betterments and major remodeling costs are capitalized. Leasehold
improvements are capitalized and amortized over the shorter of their estimated
useful lives or the terms of the respective leases. Capitalized lease
acquisition costs are being amortized over the lease terms of the underlying
leases. Costs incurred in purchasing management information systems are
capitalized and included in property and equipment. These costs are amortized
over their estimated useful lives from the date the systems become operational.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Intangible Assets and Amortization</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The costs in excess of net assets of businesses acquired are carried as
intangible assets, net of accumulated amortization, in the accompanying
consolidated balance sheets. The net intangible assets, consisting primarily of
goodwill and trade names of $352,897 as of February&nbsp;2, 2002 and $359,192 as of
February&nbsp;3, 2001, are amortized using the straight-line method over periods
ranging from 30 to 40&nbsp;years.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On February&nbsp;3, 2002, the Company adopted Statement of Financial Accounting
Standards (SFAS)&nbsp;No.&nbsp;142, &#147;Goodwill and Other Intangible Assets,&#148; and as a
result, the Company will cease to amortize the remaining goodwill. In lieu of
amortization, the Company is required to perform an initial impairment review
of its goodwill in the first six months of fiscal 2002 and an annual impairment
review thereafter.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Amortization of goodwill and trade names included in depreciation and
amortization in the accompanying consolidated statements of operations is
$12,682, $12,593 and $5,148 during fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively.
Accumulated amortization at February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001 was $74,974
and $62,292, respectively.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Impairment of Long-Lived Assets</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company periodically reviews property and equipment and intangibles
(primarily goodwill) whenever events or changes in circumstances indicate that
their carrying amounts may not be recoverable or their depreciation or
amortization periods should be accelerated. The Company assesses
recoverability based on several factors, including management&#146;s intention with
respect to its stores and those stores&#146;
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">29</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>

</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS CONTINUED</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">projected undiscounted cash flows. An impairment loss is
recognized for the amount by which the carrying amount of the assets exceeds
the present value of their projected cash flows.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Deferred Charges</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Costs incurred to obtain long-term financing are amortized over the terms
of the respective debt agreements using the straight-line method, which
approximates the interest method. Unamortized costs included in other
noncurrent assets as of February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001 were $10,436 and
$1,286, respectively. Amortization expense included in interest and
amortization of deferred financing fees is $2,292, $1,557 and $389 during
fiscal 2001, 2000 and 1999, respectively.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Marketable Equity Securities</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All marketable equity securities included in other noncurrent assets are
classified as available-for-sale under SFAS No.&nbsp;115, &#147;Accounting for Certain
Investments in Debt and Equity Securities&#148;. The Company carries these
investments at fair value with unrealized gains and losses (net of taxes)
included in accumulated other comprehensive earnings, which is reflected as a
separate component of shareholders&#146; equity. Realized gains and losses are
recognized in the Company&#146;s consolidated statement of operations when the
securities are sold or impairment is considered other than temporary. The
Company reviews its equity holdings on a regular basis to evaluate whether or
not each security has experienced an other-than-temporary decline in fair
value. The Company has reviewed each of the companies&#146; financial position,
results of operations, stock price performance and various analyst research
reports and believes that the declines in fair value of its equity holdings are
temporary.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Derivative Instruments</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under an agreement expiring February&nbsp;2, 2003, the Company uses an
interest-rate swap as a derivative to modify the interest characteristics of
its outstanding floating rate long-term debt, to reduce its exposure to
fluctuations in interest rates. The Company&#146;s accounting policy is based on
its designation of such instruments as cash flow hedges. The Company does not
enter into such contracts for speculative purposes.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Revenue Recognition</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Revenue from sales of the Company&#146;s products is recognized at the time of
sale.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Readers&#146; Advantage&#153; membership entitles the customer to receive a 10
percent discount on all purchases made during the twelve-month membership
period. The annual membership fee of $25.00 is non-refundable after the first
30&nbsp;days of the membership term. Revenue is being recognized over the
twelve-month membership period based upon historical spending patterns for
Barnes &#038; Noble customers. Refunds of membership fees due to cancellations
within the first 30&nbsp;days are minimal.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sales returns (which are not significant) are recognized at the time
returns are made.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Advertising Costs</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The costs of advertising are expensed as incurred during the year pursuant
to Statement of Position 93-7, &#147;Reporting on Advertising Costs&#148;. In addition,
consideration received from vendors in conjunction with the Company&#146;s
cooperative advertising program is netted against the related expenses.
Advertising costs are charged to selling and administrative expenses.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">30</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS CONTINUED</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2"><I>Pre-Opening Expenses</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In April 1998, the Accounting Standards Executive Committee issued
Statement of Position 98-5, &#147;Reporting on the Costs of Start-Up Activities&#148;
(SOP 98-5). SOP 98-5 requires an entity to expense all start-up activities, as
defined, when incurred. Prior to 1999, the Company amortized costs associated
with the opening of new stores over the respective store&#146;s first 12&nbsp;months of
operations. In accordance with SOP 98-5, the Company recorded a one-time
non-cash charge reflecting the cumulative effect of a change in accounting
principle in the amount of $4,500 after taxes, representing such start-up costs
capitalized as of the beginning of fiscal year 1999. Since adoption, the
Company has expensed all such start-up costs as incurred. The effect of the
change in accounting principle on earnings in fiscal 2001, fiscal 2000 and
fiscal 1999 was immaterial.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Closed Store Expenses</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Upon a formal decision to close or relocate a store, the Company charges
unrecoverable costs to expense. Such costs include the net book value of
abandoned fixtures and leasehold improvements and a provision for future lease
obligations, net of expected sublease recoveries. Costs associated with store
closings of $9,831, $5,026 and $5,447 during fiscal 2001, fiscal 2000 and
fiscal 1999, respectively, are included in selling and administrative expenses
in the accompanying consolidated statements of operations.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Net Earnings Per Common Share</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Basic earnings per share is computed by dividing income available to
common shareholders by the weighted-average number of common shares
outstanding. Diluted earnings per share reflect, in periods in which they have
a dilutive effect, the impact of common shares issuable upon exercise of its
stock options and those of its GameStop subsidiary, and assumes the conversion
of the Company&#146;s 5.25% convertible subordinated notes for the period
outstanding since their issuance in March 2001.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Income Taxes</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The provision for income taxes includes federal, state and local income
taxes currently payable and those deferred because of temporary differences
between the financial statement and tax bases of assets and liabilities. The
deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured using the enacted tax rates
and laws that are expected to be in effect when the differences reverse.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2"><I>Stock Options</I>
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company accounts for all transactions under which employees receive
shares of stock or other equity instruments in the Company or the Company
incurs liabilities to employees in amounts based on the price of its stock in
accordance with the provisions of Accounting Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;25,
&#147;Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees.&#148;
</FONT>

Saturday closest to the last day of January. The reporting periods ended
February&nbsp;2, 2002, February&nbsp;3, 2001 and January&nbsp;29, 2000 contained 52&nbsp;weeks, 53
weeks and 52&nbsp;weeks, respectively.

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>3. Debt</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On November&nbsp;18, 1997, the Company obtained an $850,000 five-year senior
revolving credit facility (the Revolving Credit Facility) with a syndicate led
by The Chase Manhattan Bank. The Revolving Credit Facility permits borrowings
at various interest-rate options based on the prime rate or London Interbank
Offer Rate (LIBOR)&nbsp;depending upon certain financial tests. In addition, the
agreement requires the Company to pay a commitment fee up to 0.25&nbsp;percent of
the unused portion depending upon certain financial tests. The Revolving Credit
Facility contains covenants, limitations and events of default typical of
credit facilities of this size and nature, including financial covenants which
require the Company to meet, among other things, cash flow and
interest-coverage ratios and which limit capital expenditures. The Revolving
Credit Facility is secured by the capital stock, accounts receivable and
general intangibles of the Company&#146;s subsidiaries. Net proceeds from the
Revolving Credit Facility are available for general corporate purposes.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2000, the Company obtained an additional $100,000 senior
unsecured seasonal credit facility (seasonal credit facility) with a syndicate
of banks led by The Chase Manhattan Bank. The seasonal credit facility, which
matured on January&nbsp;31, 2001, provided for borrowings at an interest rate based
on LIBOR. In addition, the agreement required the Company to pay a commitment
fee of 0.375&nbsp;percent of the unused portion. The seasonal credit facility was
guaranteed by all restricted subsidiaries of Barnes &#038; Noble.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">32</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS CONTINUED</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 2001, the Company issued $300,000, 5.25&nbsp;percent convertible
subordinated notes due March&nbsp;15, 2009. The notes are convertible into the
Company&#146;s common stock at a conversion price of $32.512 per share.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company from time to time enters into interest rate swap agreements to
manage interest-costs and risk associated with changes in interest rates. These
agreements effectively convert underlying variable-rate debt based on prime
rate or LIBOR to fixed-rate debt through the exchange of fixed and floating
interest payment obligations without the exchange of underlying principal
amounts. For each of the years ended February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001, the
Company had outstanding $55,000 of swaps, maturing in 2003.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>4. Fair Values of Financial Instruments</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The carrying values of cash and cash equivalents reported in the
accompanying consolidated balance sheets approximate fair value due to the
short-term maturities of these assets. The aggregate fair value of the
Revolving Credit Facility approximates its carrying amount, because of its
recent and frequent repricing based upon market conditions. Investments in
publicly traded securities accounted for under SFAS 115 are carried at fair
value.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Interest-rate swap agreements are valued based on market quotes obtained
from dealers. The estimated fair value of the interest-rate swaps liability was
$2,256 and $542 at February&nbsp;2, 2002 and February&nbsp;3, 2001, respectively. The
interest-rate swaps are included as a component of other long-term liabilities.

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>7. Net Earnings (Loss) Per Share</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Following is a reconciliation of net earnings (loss)&nbsp;and weighted average
common shares outstanding for purposes of calculating basic and diluted net
earnings per share:

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>8. Barnes &#038; Noble.com</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On November&nbsp;12, 1998, the Company and Bertelsmann AG (Bertelsmann)
completed the formation of a limited liability company to operate the online
retail bookselling operations of the Company&#146;s wholly owned subsidiary,
barnesandnoble.com inc. The new entity, barnesandnoble.com llc (Barnes &#038;
Noble.com), was structured as a limited liability company. Under the terms of
the relevant agreements, effective as of October&nbsp;31, 1998, the Company and
Bertelsmann each retained a 50&nbsp;percent membership interest in Barnes &#038;
Noble.com. The Company contributed substantially all of the assets and
liabilities of its online operations to the joint venture and Bertelsmann paid
$75,000 to the Company and made a $150,000 cash contribution to the joint
venture. Bertelsmann also agreed to contribute an additional $50,000 to the
joint venture for future working capital requirements. The Company recognized a
pre-tax gain during fiscal 1998 in the amount of $126,435, of which $63,759 was
recognized in earnings based on the $75,000 received directly and $62,676
($36,351 after taxes) was reflected in additional paid-in capital based on the
Company&#146;s share of the incremental equity of the joint venture resulting from
the $150,000 Bertelsmann contribution.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On May&nbsp;25, 1999, Barnes &#038; Noble.com Inc. completed an initial public
offering (IPO)&nbsp;of 28.75&nbsp;million shares of Class&nbsp;A Common Stock and used the
proceeds to purchase a 20&nbsp;percent interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. As a result,
the Company and Bertelsmann each retained a 40&nbsp;percent interest in Barnes &#038;
Noble.com. The Company recorded an increase in additional paid-in capital of
$116,158 after
taxes representing the Company&#146;s incremental share in the equity of Barnes
&#038; Noble.com. In November</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">36</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>


<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS CONTINUED</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">2000, Barnes &#038; Noble.com acquired Fatbrain.com, Inc.
(Fatbrain), the third largest online bookseller. Barnes &#038; Noble.com issued
shares of its common stock to Fatbrain shareholders. As a result of this
merger, the Company and Bertelsmann each retained an approximate 36&nbsp;percent
interest in Barnes &#038; Noble.com. The Company will continue to account for its
investment under the equity method.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Under the terms of the November&nbsp;12, 1998 joint venture agreement between
the Company and Bertelsmann, the Company received a $25,000 payment from
Bertelsmann in connection with the IPO. The Company recognized the $25,000
pre-tax gain in fiscal 1999. The estimated fair market values of the Company&#146;s
investment in Barnes &#038; Noble.com were $109,825, $122,000 and $742,000 at
February&nbsp;2, 2002, February&nbsp;3, 2001 and January&nbsp;29, 2000, respectively.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>9. Employees&#146; Retirement and Defined Contribution Plans</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As of December&nbsp;31, 1999, substantially all employees of the Company were
covered under a noncontributory defined benefit pension plan (the Pension
Plan). As of January&nbsp;1, 2000, the Pension Plan was amended so that employees
no longer earn benefits for subsequent service. Subsequent service continues
to be the basis for vesting of benefits not yet vested at December&nbsp;31, 1999 and
the Pension Plan will continue to hold assets and pay benefits. The amendment
was treated as a curtailment in fiscal 1999 resulting in a pre-tax gain of
$14,142 which is included as a reduction of selling and administrative
expenses.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company maintains defined contribution plans (the Savings Plans) for
the benefit of substantially all employees. In addition, the Company provides
certain health care and life insurance benefits (the Postretirement Plan) to
retired employees, limited to those receiving benefits or retired as of April
1, 1993.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">37</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Settlements in the form of lump sum cash payments were made in fiscal 2001
to plan participants in exchange for their rights to receive specified pension
benefits.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The health-care cost trend rate used to measure the expected cost of the
Postretirement Plan benefits is assumed to be nine percent in 2002 declining at
one percent decrements each year through 2005 and one-half percent decrements
through 2007 to five percent in 2007 and each year thereafter. The health-care
cost trend assumption has a significant effect on the amounts reported. For
example, a one percent increase or decrease in the health-care cost trend rate
would change the accumulated postretirement benefit obligation by approximately
$216 and $191, respectively, as of February&nbsp;2, 2002, and would change the net
periodic cost by approximately $16 and $13, respectively, during fiscal 2001.
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>11. Acquisitions</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 1999, the Company acquired Babbage&#146;s Etc., one of the nation&#146;s
largest video-game and entertainment-software specialty retailers, a company
majority owned by Leonard Riggio, for $208,670. An independent Special
Committee of the Board of Directors negotiated and approved the acquisition on
behalf of the Company. The Company made an additional payment of $9,665 in
2002 due to certain financial performance targets having been met during fiscal
year 2001.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On June&nbsp;14, 2000, the Company acquired all of the outstanding shares of
Funco, Inc., a Minneapolis-based electronic games retailer for approximately
$167,560. The acquisition was accounted for by the purchase method of
accounting and, accordingly, the results of operations for the period
subsequent to the acquisition are included in the consolidated financial
statements. The excess of purchase price over the net assets acquired, in the
amount of approximately $131,400, has been recorded as goodwill and is being
amortized using the straight-line method over an estimated useful life of 30
years. The pro forma effect assuming the acquisition of Funco, Inc. at the
beginning of fiscal 2000 is not material.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">41</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS CONTINUED</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Through a corporate restructuring, Babbage&#146;s Etc. became a wholly owned
subsidiary of Funco, Inc. and the name of Funco, Inc. was changed to GameStop,
Inc.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On February&nbsp;19, 2002, the Company successfully completed an initial public
offering for its GameStop subsidiary, raising $250,000 in cash for Barnes &#038;
Noble, Inc. and $98,000 in net proceeds for GameStop. Barnes &#038; Noble has
retained an approximate 63&nbsp;percent interest in GameStop.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>12. Segment Information</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company operates under two strategic groups that offer different
products. These groups have been aggregated into two reportable operating
segments: bookstores and video-game and entertainment-software stores.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Bookstores&nbsp;</I><BR>
</FONT>

<FONT SIZE="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This
segment includes 591 bookstores under the Barnes &#038; Noble Booksellers,
Bookstop and Bookstar names which generally offer a comprehensive title base, a
caf&#233;, a children&#146;s section, a music department, a magazine section and a
calendar of ongoing events, including author appearances and children&#146;s
activities. This segment also includes 305 small format mall-based stores
under the B. Dalton Bookseller, Doubleday Book Shops and Scribner&#146;s Bookstore
trade names. Additionally, this segment includes the operations of Calendar
Club, the Company&#146;s majority-owned subsidiary. Calendar Club is an operator of
seasonal calendar kiosks. The bookstore segment employs a merchandising
strategy that targets the &#147;Middle American&#148; consumer book market.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Video-Game
and Entertainment-Software Stores&nbsp;</I><BR>
</FONT>
<FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This
segment includes 432 Video Game &#038; Entertainment Software stores under
the Babbage&#146;s and Software Etc. names, 606 stores operated under the GameStop
and FuncoLand names, a Web site (gamestop.com) and <I>Game Informer </I>magazine. The
principal products of these stores are comprised of video-game hardware and
software and PC-entertainment software. The Company&#146;s consolidated financial
statements reflect the results of Babbage&#146;s Etc. from October 1999 and Funco,
Inc. from June 2000, the respective dates of acquisition.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The accounting policies of the segments are the same as those described in
the summary of significant accounting policies. Segment operating profit
includes corporate expenses in each operating segment. Barnes &#038; Noble
evaluates the performance of its segments and allocates resources to them based
on operating profit.
</FONT>

<P align="center"><FONT size="2">42</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>14.</B>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Shareholders&#146; Equity</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In fiscal 1999, the Board of Directors authorized a common stock
repurchase program for the purchase of up to $250,000 of the Company&#146;s common
shares. As of February&nbsp;2, 2002, the Company has repurchased 5,504,700 shares at
a cost of approximately $117,377 under this program. The repurchased shares
are held in treasury.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Each share of the Company&#146;s Common Stock also entitles the holder to the
right (the Right) to purchase one four-hundredth of a share of the Company&#146;s
Series&nbsp;H Preferred Stock for $225. The Right is only exercisable if a person
or group acquires 15&nbsp;percent or more of the Company&#146;s outstanding Common Stock
or announces a tender offer or exchange offer, the consummation of which would
result in such person or group owning 15&nbsp;percent or more of the Company&#146;s
outstanding Common Stock.
</FONT>
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">44</FONT>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always">&nbsp;</H5><P>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>NOTES TO CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS CONTINUED</B>
</FONT>

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>15.</B>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Impairment Charge</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During fiscal 2000, the Company recorded a non-cash charge to operating
earnings of $106,833. This charge included approximately $69,928 of goodwill
and $32,405 of property, plant and equipment related to the book business,
primarily goodwill associated with the purchase of B. Dalton, other
mall-bookstore assets and $6,186 of warehouse equipment. The Company&#146;s
mall-based bookstores have experienced significant declines in sales and
profitability as a result of increased competition from book superstores and
Internet book retailers. In fiscal 2000, B. Dalton comparable store sales
declined (1.7%) compared with an increase in comparable store sales of 0.1% in
fiscal 1999. As a result, the anticipated future cash flows from certain stores
were no longer sufficient to recover the carrying value of the underlying
assets. Also, included in this charge were other charges of $4,500 related to
the write-off of certain investments which had continuing adverse financial
results. The estimated fair value of the assets was based on anticipated
future cash flows discounted at a rate commensurate with the risk involved.
</FONT>
<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>16.</B>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Stock Option Plans</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company currently has two incentive plans under which stock options
have been or may be granted to officers, directors and key employees of the
Company, the 1991 Employee Incentive Plan (the 1991 Plan) and the 1996
Incentive Plan (the 1996 Plan). The options to purchase common shares generally
are issued at fair market value on the date of the grant, begin vesting after
one year in 33-1/3&nbsp;percent or 25&nbsp;percent increments per year, expire 10&nbsp;years
from issuance and are conditioned upon continual employment during the vesting
period.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The 1996 Plan and the 1991 Plan allow the Company to grant options to
purchase up to 11,000,000 and 4,732,704 shares of common stock, respectively.
No more grants may be made under the 1991 Plan.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In addition to the two incentive plans, the Company has granted stock
options to certain key executives and directors. The vesting terms and
contractual lives of these grants are similar to that of the incentive plans.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In accordance with the Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.
123, &#147;Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation&#148; (SFAS 123), the Company
discloses the pro forma impact of recording compensation expense utilizing the
Black-Scholes model. The Black-Scholes option valuation model was developed
for use in estimating the fair value of traded options which have no vesting
restrictions and are fully transferable. In addition, option valuation models
require the input of highly subjective assumptions including the expected stock
price volatility. Because the Company&#146;s stock options have characteristics
significantly different from those of traded options, and because changes in
the subjective input assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate,
in management&#146;s opinion, the Black-Scholes model does not necessarily provide a
reliable measure of the fair value of its stock options.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Had compensation cost for the Company&#146;s stock option grants been
determined based on the fair value of the stock at the grant dates, the
Company&#146;s net earnings and diluted earnings per share for fiscal 2001, 2000 and
1999, would have been reduced by approximately $9,521 or $0.12 per share,
$8,529 or $0.13 per share, and $6,298 or $0.09 per share, respectively.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Because the application of the pro forma disclosure provision of SFAS 123
are required only to be applied to grants of options made by the Company during
fiscal 1995 and after, the above pro forma amounts may not be representative of
the effects of applying SFAS 123 to future years.
</FONT>
<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The weighted-average fair value of the options granted during fiscal 2001,
2000 and 1999 were
estimated at $10.13, $7.86 and $10.00, respectively, using the Black-Scholes
option-pricing model with the following assumptions: volatility of 35&nbsp;percent,
risk-free interest rate of 4.86&nbsp;percent in fiscal 2001,
<P align="center"><FONT size="2">45</FONT>

2000, and 5.90&nbsp;percent in fiscal 1999, and an expected life of six years.

<P align="left"><FONT size="2"><B>17.</B>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<B>Leases</B>
</FONT>

<P><FONT size="2">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company leases retail stores, warehouse facilities, office space and
equipment. Substantially all of the retail stores are leased under
noncancelable agreements which expire at various dates through 2036 with
various renewal options for additional periods. The agreements, which have been
classified as operating leases, generally provide for both minimum and
percentage rentals and require the Company to pay all insurance, taxes and
other maintenance costs. Percentage rentals are based on sales performance in
excess of specified minimums at various stores.
</FONT>
